# Digital Filter Analysis and Design

## 1. A filter has a transfer function of \( $T(z) = \frac{(z - 0.1)}{(z - 0.3)}$ \) and is used with a sampling frequency of 1 kHz.

### (a) Sketch the pole-zero diagram for the filter.
- **Pole:** \( z = 0.3 \)
- **Zero:** \( z = 0.1 \)

### (b) Use your pole-zero diagram to estimate the gain and phase angle at 0 Hz and 250 Hz.

  - **Phase Angle:**
- **250 Hz:**
  - **Gain:**

### (c) Check the gain and phase angle at 250 Hz directly from the transfer function. Also use this method to find the gain and phase angle at 375 Hz.
- **Gain and Phase at 250 Hz:**
- **Gain and Phase at 375 Hz:**

## 2. A continuous filter has a transfer function, \( T(s) \), given by \( $T(s) = \frac{(s + 2)}{(s + 1)(s + 3)}$ \).

### (a) Design a digital filter that has equivalent poles and zeros by making use of the relationship \( z = e^{sv} \). The sampling frequency is 10 Hz.
- **Poles and Zeros in z-domain:**

## 3. A digital filter has the z-domain transfer function of \( $\frac{1}{z^2 - z + 0.5}$ \).

### Sketch the pole-zero diagrams for the filter outputs when the input is:
- **(a) A unit sample sequence:**
- **(b) A discrete unit step:**

### Use the system pole-zero diagram to find the gain of the system at:
- **0 Hz:**
- **\( \frac{f_s}{4} \) (where \( f_s \) is the sampling frequency):**

## 4. By using the function \( \frac{z}{z + 1} \) as an example, explain why it is impossible for a system transfer function to have more zeros than poles.
_(Hint: Consider the response of the system to a unit sample sequence.)_

## 5. A digital filter has a transfer function of the form \( $T(z) = \frac{z^2 + 0.81}{z^2 + p^2}$ \). The filter is to have a minimum gain of -6 dB occurring at a frequency of 50 Hz. Given that the sampling frequency is 200 Hz, find the appropriate p-value.
_(Hint: First sketch a pole-zero diagram to show the zero positions.)_
